# UWorld-Anki Local Source Map

Explicit UWorld QIDs were not visible in the available sources. This file therefore uses searchable local source references: source file, local question/passsage number, and a short search anchor. The working goal is at least two references per Anki note when the available UWorld sources support it.

## AminoAcids - Classifications.txt

- Amino acids that can act as nucleophiles... 1. Serine (Ser/S) 2. Threonine (Thr/T) 3. Tyrosine (Tyr/Y) 4. Cysteine (Cys/C) 5. Lysine (Lys/K) -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 6 / search: "act serine threonine"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 10 / search: "act serine cysteine"

Carbonyl ""opens"" - forming an sp3-hybridized intermediate. 3. Proton transfers convert the... -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 10 / search: "hydrolysis protonated h2o"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 43 of 59 / search: "carbonyl forming proton"
- "When a disulfide bond is formed (SH & SH → S-S), 2 electron(s) are lost, since both SHs need to get oxidized." -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 5 / search: "electron lost oxidized"
- Acidic amino acids are negatively charged. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 46 of 59 / search: "glutamate glu are negatively charged all other amino"
- Anti-parallel β-sheets are linked together by short sequences called β-turns. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 12 of 15 / search: "amino acids linked together by peptide bonds some"
- Basic amino acids are positively charged. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 46 of 59 / search: "arginine arg are positively charged whereas those of"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 59 of 59 / search: "lysine residues are positively charged and associate with"
- Classification of charged vs. uncharged amino acids: - Charged amino acids: includes only acidic or basic (ionized) amino acids. - Uncharged amino acids: includes both polar & non-polar amino acids (non-ionizable). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 59 / search: "charged non ionizable"
- Histidine has an imidazole ring. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "histidine imidazole ring"
- In isoelectric focusing, the amino acids that make the peptide's pI high are arginine (R), lysine (K), & histidine (H). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 46 of 59 / search: "peptides arginine lysine"
- List of the aromatic amino acids: 1. Tryptophan (Trp/W) 2. Phenylalanine (Phe/F) 3. Tyrosine (Tyr/Y) -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "aromatic trp tyrosine"
- List of the basic amino acids (charged) at physiological pH (7): 1. Arginine (Arg/R) 2. Lysine (Lys/K) -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 46 of 59 / search: "charged arginine arg"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 59 of 59 / search: "charged arginine lysine"
- Parallel β-sheets are linked together by long sequences called 360° loops. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 12 of 15 / search: "amino acids linked together by peptide bonds some"
- Proteins exposed to low amounts of salt become more stable due to a greater number of ionic interactions. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 59 of 59 / search: "salt become ionic"
- The 3 amino acids capable of being phosphorylated are serine (S), threonine (T), and tyrosine (Y). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 6 / search: "serine threonine tyrosine"
- The quaternary structure of a protein is primarily stabilized through non-covalent interactions & disulfide bonds. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 31 of 59 / search: "stabilized non covalent"
- The reduction of 1 disulfide bond(s) requires the addition of 2 electron(s), since both sulfur atoms need to be reduced (S-S → SH & SH). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 52 of 59 / search: "reduction electron sulfur"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 5 / search: "reduction electron reduced"
- Under certain conditions that allow chiral amino acids to tautomerize, enols are formed as intermediates - resulting in a racemic mixture when they revert back to the ketone form. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 44 of 59 / search: "chiral mixture ketone"

## Biochemistry - Bioenergetics.txt

- Proteins with bonds that do not require inputs of energy (like ATP hydrolysis) to form are thermodynamically stable. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 13 of 59 / search: "require atp thermodynamically"
- Proteins with bonds that require inputs of energy (like ATP hydrolysis) to form are thermodynamically unstable. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 13 of 59 / search: "require atp thermodynamically"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 59 / search: "atp thermodynamically unstable"

## Biochemistry - Carbohydrates.txt

- "Glycogen phosphorylase only cleaves at the non-reducing ends of glycogen that are at least 4 monosaccharides away from a branch point." -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 26 of 30 / search: "non away branch"
- A carbohydrate in its cyclic form has 1 more chiral center than it does in its linear form. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "carbohydrate cyclic linear"
- A carbohydrate in its linear form has 1 less chiral center than it does in its cyclic form. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "carbohydrate linear cyclic"
- A carbohydrate's anomeric carbon in its cyclic form was originally its carbonyl carbon in its straight-chain form. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "carbohydrates anomeric cyclic"
- Anomers are carbohydrates that differ only by their α or β configurations. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "conformation epimers are carbohydrates that differ at only"
- Are carbohydrates mostly in the linear or cyclic form? Cyclic, since the cyclic form is more stable. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "carbohydrates linear cyclic"
- Can humans digest β-1,4 linkages of sugars? No - think of cellulose (except in the case of lactose) -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 15 / search: "humans beta lactose"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 15 / search: "humans sugars lactose"
- Cellulose is a linear homopolysaccharide made of β-D-glucose residues in a β-1,4 linkage. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "cellulose linear beta"
- D-fructose can cyclize into either a furanose or pyranose. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "cyclized sugars furanose or pyranose because in the"
- Epimers are diastereomers that differ in configuration at only 1 chiral center on carbohydrates. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 15 / search: "epimers configuration chiral"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "epimers differ carbohydrates"
- Glycosides from 5 and 6 membered rings are called... 5: furanoside 6: pyranoside -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 56 of 59 / search: "of three 6 membered rings and one 5"
- Humans cannot digest any sugars with β-linkages, apart from lactose. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 15 / search: "humans sugars apart"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 15 / search: "humans beta lactose"
- In a sugar's cyclic form, reducing sugars can be identified by the presence of a(n) free OH on its anomeric carbon. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 10 / search: "sugars reducing presence"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 8 of 15 / search: "reducing sugars can"
- In a sugar's linear form, reducing sugars can be identified by the presence of a(n) aldehyde group on C1. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 10 / search: "sugars reducing presence"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 8 of 15 / search: "reducing sugars can"
- In a Tollen's test, a silver precipitate indicates the presence of a reducing sugar in solution. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 10 / search: "tollens silver presence"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 10 / search: "tollens silver reducing"
- In Benedict's or Tollen's test, the functional group that acts as the reducing agent is the aldehyde in the sugar's linear form - getting oxidized into a carboxylic acid in the process. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 10 / search: "tollens reducing agent"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 10 / search: "tollens reducing sugars"
- In Benedict's test, fructose gives a false positive since it can tautomerize to give an aldehyde in its linear form - making it appear as a reducing sugar. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 10 / search: "fructose tautomerize reducing"
- Lactose is a disaccharide made of β-D-galactose & β-D-glucose in an β-1,4 linkage. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 15 / search: "lactose disaccharide beta"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 15 / search: "lactose disaccharide galactose"
- Maltose is a disaccharide made of α-D-glucose residues in an α-1,4 linkage. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 15 / search: "maltose disaccharide linkage"
- Mutarotation is when carbohydrates spontaneously change between α & β anomers. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "carbohydrates beta anomers"
- On a carbohydrate's ring structure, acetals always have 1 non-hydrogen & 1 H group bound to its anomeric carbon. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 15 / search: "ring bound anomeric"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "carbohydrates always anomeric"
- On a carbohydrate's ring structure, ketals always have 2 non-hydrogen groups bound to its anomeric carbon. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 15 / search: "ring bound anomeric"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "carbohydrates always anomeric"
- On a fischer projection, what does the horizontal line represent? Wedge -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "reversed in a fischer projection d sugars always"
- On a fischer projection, what does the vertical line represent? Dash -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "reversed in a fischer projection d sugars always"
- On carbohydrates, α-anomers & β-anomers do differ in optical activity. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "carbohydrates anomers beta"
- Sucrose is a disaccharide made of α-D-glucose & β-D-fructose in an α-1,2 linkage. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 10 / search: "disaccharide beta linkage"
- The S/R designation of OH or H on Fischer projections should always be inverted. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "fischer projections always"
- These sugars are held together by α-glycosidic linkages. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 10 / search: "sugars glycosidic linkages"
- These sugars are held together by β-glycosidic linkages. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 10 / search: "sugars beta glycosidic"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 15 / search: "disaccharides linked by beta glycosidic bonds the anomeric"
- To test for only glucose's presence in a solution of reducing sugars, glucose oxidase is used. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 10 / search: "presence reducing sugars"
- Tollen's reagent uses Ag(NH3)2+ to detect reducing sugars. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 10 / search: "tollens nh3 reducing"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 10 / search: "tollens reagent reducing"
- Tollens test can only detect reducing sugars in solutions of acteals, since the linear form of a ketal is instead already fully oxidized. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 10 / search: "tollens reducing sugars"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 10 / search: "tollens reducing sugars"
- What's the difference between a complex carbohydrate & a simple carbohydrate? - Complex: multiple carbohydrates (disaccharide/polysaccharide) - Simple: one carbohydrate (monosaccharide) -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 45 of 59 / search: "carbohydrate disaccharide monosaccharide"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 15 / search: "carbohydrates disaccharide monosaccharide"
- What's the difference between maltose & amylose? Maltose: disaccharide Amylose: polysaccharide -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 15 / search: "maltose disaccharide polysaccharide"
- When drawing a carbohydrate's fischer projection into a ring, OH's on the fischer projection... Right: point down Left: point up -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "structures represents the fischer projection of a beta"
- When drawing a carbohydrate's fischer projection into a ring, OHs on the fischer projection... Left: point up Right: point down -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "structures represents the fischer projection of a beta"
- When the highest number stereocenter (C5) on a cyclic carbohydrate is R, the linear carbohydrate is D. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "stereocenter cyclic carbohydrate"
- When the highest number stereocenter (C5) on a cyclic carbohydrate is S, the linear carbohydrate is L. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "stereocenter cyclic carbohydrate"
- α-D-glucose & β-D-glucose are epimers & anomers of each other. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "beta epimers anomers"

- A(n) acrocentric centromere position is when the centromere is located very off-center (very short p arm). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 24 of 30 / search: "located center short"
- After DNA polymerase adds a base to the growing strand, pyrophosphate is released. -> Local sources: 06-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q.pdf / Question 7 of 30 / search: "happens when dna polymerase adds a deoxyribonucleotide triphosphate"; 08-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q-Results-Merge.pdf / Question 7 of 30 / search: "happens when dna polymerase adds a deoxyribonucleotide triphosphate"
- Bacterial genomes use DNA methylase to methylate their own DNA during replication - allowing them to differentiate between their own DNA and foreign DNA (i.e. viral). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 18 of 59 / search: "allowing differentiate foreign"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "replication foreign viral"
- cDNA is DNA made from mRNA transcripts, meaning it can bind directly to DNA's sense-strand. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "cdna mrna strand"
- cDNA is synthesized from an mRNA transcript via the action of reverse transcriptase. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "cdna mrna transcript"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 40 of 59 / search: "mrna reverse transcriptase"
- cDNA libraries are made by reverse-transcribing mRNA back into its original DNA. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "cdna reverse mrna"
- Chain-terminating method of DNA sequencing incorporates ddNTPs into the growing DNA strand to terminate its growth. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 6 / search: "terminating sequencing ddntps"
- Cuts from restriction enzymes can create sticky ends, which reanneal easily. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "restriction sticky ends"

- DNA helicase separates the double helix by breaking hydrogen bonds. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 31 of 59 / search: "double helix hydrogen"
- DNA libraries are generated by randomly fragmenting DNA and cloning the fragments into a vector. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 30 / search: "generated cloning vector"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 30 / search: "generated cloning vector"
- DNA polymerase travels along the parent strand in the 3' → 5' direction but synthesizes its transcript in the 5' → 3' direction. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "polymerase strand transcript"
- DNA's double helix is stabilized by hydrogen bonding & planar base (π) stacking. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 31 of 59 / search: "double helix stabilized"

- For multimeric proteins that are linked together by disulfide bonds, native/non-reducing SDS-PAGE will not separate their subunits into monomers - resulting in shorter migration distances. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 12 of 15 / search: "amino acids linked together by peptide bonds some"
- For multimeric proteins that are not linked together by disulfide bonds, non-reducing SDS-PAGE will separate their subunits into monomers - resulting in further migration distances. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 12 of 15 / search: "amino acids linked together by peptide bonds some"
- For two strands of DNA with equal G:C contents, the strand with the G:C base pairs located near the ends of the strand are stronger. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 31 of 59 / search: "strands strand pairs"
- For two strands of DNA with equal G:C contents, the strand with the G:C base pairs located near the middle of the strand are weaker. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 31 of 59 / search: "strands strand pairs"
- Guanine has 2 hydrogen bond donors & cytosine has 2 hydrogen bond acceptors. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 31 of 59 / search: "guanine hydrogen cytosine"
- Histone acetylation can be detected by a Western blot, since those are capable of detecting proteins & protein modifications. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 15 / search: "choice b a western blot using an antibody"
- Histone proteins are positively charged due to their basic amino acids. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 59 / search: "histone positively charged"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 46 of 59 / search: "arginine arg are positively charged whereas those of"
- Homologous recombination repairs double-stranded breaks in DNA by using its sister chromatid's sequence as a template. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 12 of 30 / search: "double stranded breaks"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 14 of 30 / search: "double stranded breaks"
- How does the chain-terminating method of DNA sequencing work? DNA strands separated by heating → ddNTP incorporated into the growing chain → growth is terminated (due to ddNTP) → differently sized fragments separated via gel electrophoresis -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 6 / search: "terminating sequencing ddntp"

- In DNA replication, ligase only reconnects the phosphodiester backbone - it does not lay down nucleotides. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 6 / search: "replication phosphodiester nucleotides"
- In DNA replication, the leading strand in DNA replication synthesizes in the direction of DNA helicase. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 30 / search: "replication strand helicase"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 30 / search: "replication strand helicase"
- In DNA, G:C base pairs are better at π-stacking, since their additional hydrogen bond prevents rotation and holds the conjugated π-bonds in place - yielding greater stability. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 58 of 59 / search: "since additional stability"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 31 of 59 / search: "pairs additional hydrogen"
- In gel electrophoresis, increasing the voltage will increase the speed at which the sample migrates - it will not make it migrate further. -> Local sources: 05-UWorld_Physics_05222026_IDNoID_15Q.pdf / Question 2 of 15 / search: "gel electrophoresis voltage"; 05-UWorld_Physics_05222026_IDNoID_15Q.pdf / Question 3 of 15 / search: "gel electrophoresis voltage"
- In gel electrophoresis, large DNA strands do not migrate very far in the gel. -> Local sources: 05-UWorld_Physics_05222026_IDNoID_15Q.pdf / Question 2 of 15 / search: "gel electrophoresis migrate"; 05-UWorld_Physics_05222026_IDNoID_15Q.pdf / Question 3 of 15 / search: "gel electrophoresis migrate"
- In gel electrophoresis, short DNA strands migrate further in the gel. -> Local sources: 05-UWorld_Physics_05222026_IDNoID_15Q.pdf / Question 2 of 15 / search: "gel electrophoresis migrate"; 05-UWorld_Physics_05222026_IDNoID_15Q.pdf / Question 3 of 15 / search: "gel electrophoresis migrate"
- In order for a point mutation to be visualized with a Southern blot, the mutation must have disrupted a palindromic sequence - revealing that the mutated band was unable to be cleaved by a restriction enzyme. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 6 / search: "point mutation unable"
- In PCR, 92°C separates the strands & 62°C allows the primers to anneal. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "pcr primers anneal"
- In Sanger Sequencing, ddNTPs are incorporated into the growing strand to terminate its growth, due to the fact that it lacks a C3' OH - preventing the formation of the phosphodiester bond. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 6 / search: "sanger sequencing ddntps"
- In the lab, RT-PCR can be used to quantify mRNA levels by measuring the amount of resulting cDNA. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "pcr mrna cdna"
- Intergenic regions of DNA are non-coding sequences that separate genes from each other. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 30 / search: "coding sequences genes"

- RT-PCR first synthesizes cDNA from an mRNA template using reverse transcriptase, which it amplifies into many copies of double-stranded DNA. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 40 of 59 / search: "rna into double stranded dna and the viral"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "pcr cdna mrna"
- Southern blots uses single-stranded DNA as a probe & detect the target DNA's presence by whether it binds its complement. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "uses stranded target"
- Steps to determining if a ring is aromatic using Hückel's rule: 1. Plug the number of π-electrons (2 per π-bond) into 4n+2 = π-electrons. 2. Solve for n. 3. If n is a whole number, the compound is aromatic. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "ring aromatic solve"
- Telomerase extends DNA's lagging strand by synthesizing an overhang made of complementary RNA and allowing DNA polymerase to synthesize its complement. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "strand complementary polymerase"
- The chain-terminating method of DNA sequencing is also referred to as Sanger sequencing. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 6 / search: "terminating sequencing sanger"
- The hydrogen bonding that takes place between complementary DNA strands is due to interactions between the functional groups of the nitrogenous bases (A, T, C, G). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 59 of 59 / search: "rather than the nitrogenous bases on b the"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 59 / search: "not with the nitrogenous bases furthermore a strengthened"
- The nitrogenous bases (adenine, thymine, guanine, cytosine) are aromatic. -> Local sources: 06-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q.pdf / Question 7 of 30 / search: "the five nitrogenous bases adenine cytosine guanine thymine"; 08-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q-Results-Merge.pdf / Question 7 of 30 / search: "the five nitrogenous bases adenine cytosine guanine thymine"
- Thymine dimers cause double-stranded breaks in DNA. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 31 of 59 / search: "thymine double stranded"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 12 of 30 / search: "double stranded breaks"

## Biochemistry - RNA Gene Expression.txt

- "The TATA box is typically located -25 bases upstream from where RNA polymerase begins synthesizing its mRNA transcript." -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "polymerase mrna transcript"

- A non-conservative point mutation in DNA is one where the category (acidic, basic, polar, etc.) of the resulting amino acid is changed. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 6 / search: "a single point mutation in which the fourth"

- Cystic fibrosis results from a frameshift mutation in a codon encoding phenylalanine - resulting in a defective Cl- channel that never exits the endoplasmic reticulum. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 6 / search: "cystic fibrosis mutation"
- DNA methylase adds methyl groups to adenine & cytosine nucleotides on DNA - silencing gene transcription. -> Local sources: 06-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q.pdf / Question 7 of 30 / search: "adds adenine cytosine"; 08-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q-Results-Merge.pdf / Question 7 of 30 / search: "adds adenine cytosine"
- During translation, the mRNA's codon & tRNA's anti-codon base-pair in a(n) antiparallel direction. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 25 of 30 / search: "translation mrnas trnas"
- Histone acetylases add acetyl groups to lysine residues on histone tails - neutralizing the histone's charge & causing it to unwind from DNA. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 59 / search: "histone lysine residues"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 59 of 59 / search: "acetyl lysine residues"
- Histone deacetylases remove acetyl groups from lysine residues on histone tails - restoring the histone's charge & causing it to tighten around DNA. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 59 / search: "histone remove lysine"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 59 of 59 / search: "acetyl lysine residues"
- In a prokaryotic operon, the regulator gene encodes for the repressor/inducer protein that binds to the operator site & regulates transcription. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 6 / search: "regulator site regulates"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 47 of 59 / search: "regulator site transcription"
- In mRNA, the sequences for stop codons are UAA, UAG, and UGA. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 30 / search: "mrna sequences codons"
- In order for DNA's enhancer region & promoter region to come into contact with each other, DNA has to bend itself into a hairpin loop. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 32 of 59 / search: "enhancer promoter contact"
- In prokaryotes, mRNA is polycistronic - meaning it carries the information for multiple genes to encode multiple proteins. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 30 / search: "mrna genes encode"
- In repressible operons, repressor proteins cannot function until a corepressor binds - shutting off transcription once they both bind to the promoter. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 32 of 59 / search: "repressor transcription promoter"
- In the initiation phase of translation, the ribosome's small subunit first attaches to the mRNA transcript's 5' end. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 25 of 30 / search: "translation ribosomes mrna"
- In the lac operon, catabolite activator protein (CAP) stimulates gene transcription by binding to the operator & recruiting RNA polymerase to the promoter site. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 32 of 59 / search: "activator transcription promoter"
- In the ribosome, the P site is where peptidyl transferase (apart of the large subunit) catalyzes the formation of peptide bonds using GTP hydrolysis. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 10 / search: "site peptide hydrolysis"
- Mutations that take place on the wobble position of a codon are usually silent mutations, since the amino acid it codes for is often unchanged. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 30 / search: "wobble codon silent"
- On a tRNA molecule, 1 anticodon can recognize multiple different codon(s). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 30 / search: "trna anticodon codon"
- On DNA, silencer regions are sequences that contain repressor proteins that prevent RNA polymerase from binding to the promoter sequence. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 32 of 59 / search: "sequences repressor promoter"
- Polyadenylate polymerase catalyzes the addition of adenine residues to pre-mRNA to form the 3' poly-A tail - powered by ATP hydrolysis. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "polymerase mrna poly"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 25 of 30 / search: "mrna poly tail"
- Pre-mRNA transcripts are shorter in length than the original gene, due to the lack of regulatory sequences (i.e. promoter region). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 32 of 59 / search: "mrna sequences promoter"
- Response elements are specific DNA sequences located in its promoter region that allow the binding of only very specific transcription factors. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 32 of 59 / search: "sequences promoter transcription"
- RNA polymease attaches to DNA's antisense strand to model the mRNA transcript after the sense strand. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "strand mrna transcript"
- RNA polymerase catalyzes the transcription of the mRNA transcript from DNA's template strand. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "polymerase mrna transcript"
- RNA polymerase travels along DNA's antisense strand in the 3' → 5' direction to synthesize its transcript in the 5' → 3' direction. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "polymerase strand transcript"
- Sense mRNA (5' → 3') is identical in sequence (apart from uracil) to DNA's coding (5' → 3') strand. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 31 of 59 / search: "mrna uracil strand"
- Structural differences between miRNA and siRNA... miRNA: single-stranded hairpin loop. siRNA: double-stranded RNA. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 31 of 59 / search: "structural stranded double"
- Structural differences between miRNA and siRNA... siRNA: double-stranded RNA. miRNA: single-stranded hairpin loop. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 31 of 59 / search: "structural double stranded"
- The 3'-tail added to the hnRNA transcript serves to limit mRNA's time in the cytosol, since its residues slowly degrade over time. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 25 of 30 / search: "tail added mrnas"
- The 5'-cap added to the hnRNA transcript allows the future mRNA to both survive longer in the cytoplasm & get recognized by ribosomes. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "transcript mrna cytoplasm"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 25 of 30 / search: "added mrna ribosomes"
- The DNA-binding domain on transcription factors binds to specific DNA sequences within the promoter region. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 32 of 59 / search: "transcription sequences promoter"
- The genetic code is degenerate, meaning more than 1 codon can specify for the same amino acid. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 30 / search: "code degenerate codon"
- The mRNA transcript has untranslated regions on both its 3' & 5' ends, since the ribosome only translates from AUG → stop codon. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "mrna transcript ends"
- The promoter region's TATA box has a high concentration of adenine & thymine residues, since having a fewer number of hydrogen bonds makes strand separation easier. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 31 of 59 / search: "adenine thymine hydrogen"; 06-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q.pdf / Question 7 of 30 / search: "adenine thymine strand"
- The wobble effect is explained by the fact that the 3rd base pair on a codon experiences non-Watson & Crick binding, meaning it can bind even if the last base doesn't match. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 30 / search: "wobble codon watson"
- To control for autophoshorylation, researchers should incubate the enzyme with ATP (excluding the substrate) in order to measure the level of phosphorylation associated with just the enzyme itself. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 49 of 59 / search: "atp substrate phosphorylation"
- Transcription factors are translated in the cytoplasm but wait in the nucleus until they're needed to regulate gene transcription. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 40 of 59 / search: "transcription translated cytoplasm"
- When miRNAs are perfectly complementary to an mRNA transcript, they silence the transcript's expression by cleaving it. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "complementary mrna transcript"
- When miRNAs are somewhat complementary to an mRNA transcript, they silence the transcript's expression by preventing translation. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "complementary mrna transcript"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 25 of 30 / search: "complementary mrna translation"

## Biology - Cells.txt

- Ameoba & paramecium are single-celled eukaryotes that replicate through binary fission. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 41 of 59 / search: "celled binary fission"

## Biology - Genetics Evolution.txt

- 5-bromouracil (5-BU) is a base analog that resembles uracil - pairing best with adenine in its keto form & pairing best with guanine in its enol form. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 31 of 59 / search: "uracil adenine guanine"; 06-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q.pdf / Question 7 of 30 / search: "uracil adenine guanine"
- Adaptive radiation describes the rapid rise in the number of different species derived from one common ancestor - lacking the ability to interbreed. -> Local sources: Digestion Excretion Passages.docx / Passage 4 / search: "regulates the adaptive cellular response to hypoxia and"
- Convergent evolution is when distantly-related species evolve similar phenotypes. -> Local sources: Digestion Excretion Passages.docx / Question 10 / search: "nontoxic substances similar amounts of nontoxic ferrocyanide are"
- Genes that have arisen from the same common ancestor & with identical sequences are homologous genes. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 56 of 59 / search: "genes arisen sequences"
- In a test cross, if only the allele from one specific parent (only the father or only the mother) is resulting in the expression of the gene, it follows a(n) imprinted inheritence pattern. -> Local sources: Digestion Excretion Passages.docx / Passage 4 / search: "the consequent expression of tight junction proteins researchers"
- In evolution, commensalism is a type of symbiosis where 1 species benefits & 1 species is unaffected. -> Local sources: Digestion Excretion Passages.docx / Passage 2 / search: "aquatic environment where there is a higher external"
- In evolution, homologous structures are two structures that have similar evolutionary histories and have different function(s). -> Local sources: Digestion Excretion Discretes.docx / Question 26 / search: "exhibit an evolutionary adaptation that allows them to"
- In evolution, parasitism is a type of symbiosis where 1 species benefits & 1 species is harmed. -> Local sources: Digestion Excretion Passages.docx / Passage 2 / search: "aquatic environment where there is a higher external"
- In gene mapping, the recombination frequency (θ) represents the likelihood that two alleles will be separated from each other after crossing-over finishes. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 20 / search: "frequency represents separated"
- In genetics, variable expressivity means that the patients with one particular genotype will manifest the phenotype in different ways. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 26 of 59 / search: "variable expressivity particular"
- In non-Mendelian genetics, polygenes are multiple genes that interact with each other to influence the expression of a particular phenotype. -> Local sources: Digestion Excretion Passages.docx / Passage 4 / search: "the consequent expression of tight junction proteins researchers"
- Starting from a common ancestor, parallel evolution is when two lineagaes split apart and form similar characteristics due to having similar environments. -> Local sources: Digestion Excretion Discretes.docx / Question 26 / search: "water deficient environments and exhibit an evolutionary adaptation"
- Why are test crosses always done between the unknown individual and a known homozygous recessive individual? If a trait is recessive, it's easy to tell the genotype of the inidividual based on their recessive phenotype - you can just look. ## Biology - Musculoskeletal System.txt

Each muscle fiber might have a different concentration of actin/myosin. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 49 of 59 / search: "muscle actin myosin"
- Cardiac & smooth muscles are innervated by the autonomic nervous system. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 26 of 30 / search: "spent explanation the autonomic nervous system comprising the"; Digestion Excretion Discretes.docx / Question 17 / search: "that increase smooth muscle contractions throughout the gl"

- Different muscle fibers in the same motor unit can produce different contractile strengths, since each might differ in their concentrations of actin or myosin. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 49 of 59 / search: "muscle actin myosin"

## General Chemistry - Gases.txt

- According to Henry's law, lower partial pressures (Pgas) of a gas above a liquid surface means the concentration of the gas is higher in the solution. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 59 / search: "pressures gas liquid"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 11 of 59 / search: "pressures gas liquid"
- According to the kinetic theory of gases, the collisions of gas molecules are perfectly elastic, meaning no energy is lost (heat). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "gases gas lost"
- Dalton's law says the total pressure (PT) of all the different gases in a mixture is equal to the sum of the partial pressures of each different gas. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 11 of 59 / search: "mixture pressures gas"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 15 of 59 / search: "d if the partial pressures of the reactants"
- Gas molecules of different masses exert the same pressure against the container walls. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "gas exert container"
- Gas pressure is the amount of force per area gas molecules exert on the container walls. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "gas area exert"
- Heavier gas molecules have more momentum and exert more force against the container walls. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "gas exert container"
- High pressures cause gases to act more real, since the gas molecules are forced into close proximity - leading to stronger attractive intermolecular forces. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 5 / search: "close proximity attractive"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 13 of 59 / search: "pressures gas stronger"
- In fluid barometers, the liquid inside the tube rises until the total pressure inside (Pliquid + Pempty air) is equal to the atmospheric pressure (Patm) outside the tube. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "an area atmospheric pressure patm refers to the"
- In fluid barometers, when the Patm is higher outside the tube than the total pressure (Pliquid + Pempty air) inside the tube, the height of the fluid rises to reach equilibrium. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "patm tube inside"
- In fluid barometers, when the Patm is lower outside the tube than the total pressure (Pliquid + Pempty air) inside the tube, the height of the fluid drops to reach equilibrium. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "patm tube inside"
- In gases, collision force is the force exerted by a gas molecule on another gas molecule with the wall. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "gases exerted gas"
- In the ideal gas equation, T should always be in Kelvin (K). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "ideal gas kelvin"
- Ions (cations or anions) are highly unstable in the gas phase. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 59 / search: "highly unstable gas"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 11 of 59 / search: "highly unstable gas"
- Lighter gas molecules have less momentum and exert less force against the container walls. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "gas exert container"
- Real gases exert lower pressures on the container walls than ideal gases due to their slight intermolecular forces. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "gases exert container"
- Thermometers work when atmospheric gas molecules collide with the glass and transfer their kinetic energy to gas molecules inside - raising the liquid. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "work gas transfer"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "atmospheric gas inside"
- When the pressure of a gas is significantly increased & the volume is significantly decreased... - Gases experience attractive intermolecular forces. - Volume of the individual gas molecules becomes more significant. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 5 / search: "attractive intermolecular forces"

## General Chemistry - Redox Inorganic Reactions.txt

- Combustion reactions use a hydrocarbon & an oxidant as reactants and always form CO2 & H2O as products. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 15 of 59 / search: "combustion reactants co2"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 5 / search: "reactants always h2o"

- Reduction is the gain of electrons. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 5 / search: "signals a gain of electrons reduction a change"
- Steps to find the net reaction: 1. Multiply each reactant by whatever number needed to make the electrons equal (5e- & 2e-→ 10e-). 2. Combine the reactants into one large equation. 3. Simplify the coefficients by dividing by a common denominator (if possible). -> Local sources: 06-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q.pdf / Question 5 of 30 / search: "steps needed coefficients"; 06-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q.pdf / Question 6 of 30 / search: "steps reactant reactants"

- In Raoult's law where solute-solute and solvent-solvent interactions are equal to solute-solvent interactions, vapor pressure will be accurate to what the law predicts. -> Local sources: 06-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q.pdf / Question 4 of 30 / search: "of the solute and solvent in solutions 1"; 08-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q-Results-Merge.pdf / Question 4 of 30 / search: "of the solute and solvent in solutions 1"
- In Raoult's law where solute-solute and solvent-solvent interactions are stronger than solute-solvent interactions, vapor pressure will be higher than what the law predicts. -> Local sources: 06-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q.pdf / Question 4 of 30 / search: "of the solute and solvent in solutions 1"; 08-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q-Results-Merge.pdf / Question 4 of 30 / search: "of the solute and solvent in solutions 1"
- In Raoult's law where solute-solute and solvent-solvent interactions are weaker than solute-solvent interactions, vapor pressure will be lower than what the law predicts. -> Local sources: 06-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q.pdf / Question 4 of 30 / search: "of the solute and solvent in solutions 1"; 08-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q-Results-Merge.pdf / Question 4 of 30 / search: "of the solute and solvent in solutions 1"

- In isothermal processes, heat transfer (Q) between the system and surroundings can happen - the internal energy (U) is always zero, so the heat added (Q) must cancel out work (W) done by the system. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "heat transfer internal"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 8 of 10 / search: "heat work done"

- Mechanism of keto-enol tautomerization in acidic conditions: 1. Ketone's oxygen is protonated by H3O+. 2. π-electrons move onto the oxygen to form OH. 3. H2O deprotonates the α-carbon to form the adjacent double bond. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 10 / search: "protonated h3o h2o"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 40 of 59 / search: "mechanism move double"
- Mechanism of keto-enol tautomerization in basic conditions: 1. Ketone's α-carbon is deprotonated by OH-- forming the adjacent double bond 2. π-electrons move onto the oxygen to form O-. 3. O- deprotonates H2O to form OH. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 43 of 59 / search: "forming adjacent double"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 40 of 59 / search: "mechanism double move"
- The formation of acetals/ketals from hemiacetals/hemiketals proceeds as an SN1 nucleophilic substitution. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 57 of 59 / search: "sn1 nucleophilic substitution"
- The α-carbon adjacent to a carbonyl is highly acidic due to both the weakness of its C-H bonds and its highly stable conjugate base (enolate). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 43 of 59 / search: "adjacent carbonyl conjugate"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 42 of 59 / search: "carbonyl conjugate enolate"

## Organic Chemistry - Common Organic Reactions.txt

- Aldehydes & ketones can temporarily be turned into acetals or ketals for protection from oxidants or reducing agents. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 10 / search: "aldehydes ketones reducing"
- Alkylation is the process of adding an alkyl group (R-) to nitrogen atoms during amine synthesis. Overalkylation occurs when more than one alkyl group is added to nitrogen, leading to secondary amines (R2NH) or tertiary amines (R3N) instead of the desired p... -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 48 of 59 / search: "alkyl amine secondary"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "alkyl nitrogen amines"
- Amines & amides act as bases due to the lone pair on their nitrogen atoms. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "amines amides nitrogen"
- Amines and amides can only be ionized by strong acids. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "reactions 12 amines and amides subject unit chapter"
- BH3/THF acts as a reducing agent that prioritizes carboxylic acids first. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 10 / search: "reducing agent carboxylic"
- Copper (Cu) acts as a(n) reducing agent, since it can easily oxidize itself into Cu2+. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 10 / search: "reducing agent oxidize"
- DIBAL is a(n) reducing agent that's capable of converting carboxylic acids/esters into aldehydes. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 10 / search: "reducing agent carboxylic"
- Free radicals are compounds with an odd number of valence electrons & a(n) incomplete octet - leading to high reactivity. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 58 of 59 / search: "valence electrons a"
- In intramolecular esterification reactions, the carbonyl carbon is initially reduced to an alcohol after being attacked, but it eventually reforms the carbonyl in the final cyclic product. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 43 of 59 / search: "intramolecular carbonyl final"
- In the Williamson ether synthesis, the strong base (NaH) deprotonates the alcohol to make it more nucleophilic to attack the alkyl-halide (MeI). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 43 of 59 / search: "nucleophilic attack alkyl"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 58 of 59 / search: "nucleophilic attack alkyl"
- Michael addition reactions are when enolates nucleophilically attack the β-carbons of π-bonds adjacent to a carbonyl. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 43 of 59 / search: "michael attack beta"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 42 of 59 / search: "michael beta carbonyl"
- Oxidizing & reducing agents typically act first on the functional group with the highest priority. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 55 of 59 / search: "to provide the highest priority functional groups with"
- Rate equation for SN2 reactions... rate = k\[substrate\]\[nucleophile\] -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 56 of 59 / search: "sn2 substrate nucleophile"
- SN1 & E1 reactions prefer protic solvents since it aids in carbocation stability. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 58 of 59 / search: "sn1 since carbocation"
- SN1 reactions can sometimes take place with primary leaving groups when they're on allylic positions due to the resonance stabilization of the carbocation. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 56 of 59 / search: "sn1 leaving allylic"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 58 of 59 / search: "sn1 leaving allylic"
- SN1 reactions can sometimes take place with primary leaving groups when they're on an allylic double bond position. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 56 of 59 / search: "sn1 leaving allylic"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 57 of 59 / search: "sn1 leaving allylic"
- SN1 reactions form racemic mixtures since they form carbocation intermediates. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 58 of 59 / search: "sn1 since carbocation"
- SN1 reactions prefer tertiary 3° carbons, due to the carbocation stability. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 58 of 59 / search: "farnesyl impact the carbocation stability directly impact both"
- SN1 reactions require the formation of a carbocation before the nucleophilic attack occurs. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 58 of 59 / search: "sn1 carbocation nucleophilic"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 57 of 59 / search: "sn1 nucleophilic attack"
- SN2 reactions are limited both by the nucleophile & leaving group. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 56 of 59 / search: "sn2 nucleophile leaving"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 59 / search: "sn2 nucleophile leaving"
- Strong nucleophiles result in SN2 substitution reactions. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 56 of 59 / search: "nucleophiles sn2 substitution"
- The Robinson Annulation reaction is a combination of 2 reactions: Michael addition & aldol condensation. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 40 of 59 / search: "40 44 the robinson annulation is a three"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 42 of 59 / search: "40 44 the robinson annulation is a three"
- The α-carbon next to a carbonyl is more acidic due to the resonance stability of the enolate. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 42 of 59 / search: "carbonyl resonance enolate"
- Treating carbonyls with R-MgBr will reduce the carbonyl → alcohol & add the R-group to the old carbonyl carbon following a(n) acidic workup. -> Local sources: 06-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q.pdf / Question 24 of 30 / search: "carbonyls carbonyl acidic"; 08-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q-Results-Merge.pdf / Question 24 of 30 / search: "carbonyls carbonyl acidic"
- Weak nucleophiles result in SN1 substitution reactions. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 56 of 59 / search: "nucleophiles sn1 substitution"
- When a carboxylic acid is treated with R-MgBr, MgBr adds itself to the nucleophilic oxygen - forming O-MgBr & an alkane byproduct. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 43 of 59 / search: "adds nucleophilic forming"
- Zinc (Zn) acts as a(n) reducing agent, since it can easily oxidize itself into Zn2+. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 10 / search: "reducing agent oxidize"

## Organic Chemistry - Lab Techniques.txt

- Compounds with strong intermolecular forces are not volatile. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 5 / search: "strong intermolecular forces"
- Compounds with weak intermolecular forces are highly volatile. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 5 / search: "weak intermolecular forces"
- Equation for the charged particle's radius of curvature due to a magnetic field (B) in mass spectrometry: -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 45 of 59 / search: "if all the charged particles are to particles"
- Fluorophores are conjugated π systems that emit photons of light with less energy & larger wavelengths than what they absorbed, due to a loss of energy as heat. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 35 of 59 / search: "sample lasers emit photons of electromagnetic radiation over"
- HPLC is when non-volatile compounds are injected into a machine and carried in the liquid phase through the column under high pressures. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 47 of 59 / search: "hplc carried phase"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 49 of 59 / search: "hplc carried phase"
- In affinity chromatography for the separation of proteins, nickel lines the column to bind onto the protein's histidine residues. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 12 of 15 / search: "chromatography column histidine"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 13 of 15 / search: "chromatography column histidine"
- In affinity chromatography, affinity tags are things added to proteins that give them an affinity for compounds lining the column (intended to cause them to adhere together). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 12 of 15 / search: "chromatography column together"
- In affinity chromatography, proteins are removed from the column by pouring in more receptors that compete with the receptor its bound to. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 44 of 59 / search: "chromatography column receptor"
- In gas chromatography, compounds with lower boiling points will elute first, while higher boiling points will elute last. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 12 of 15 / search: "chromatography lower elute"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 13 of 15 / search: "chromatography lower elute"
- In gas chromatography, the stationary phase is a liquid & the mobile phase is a gas. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 44 of 59 / search: "chromatography stationary phase"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 59 / search: "chromatography stationary mobile"
- In IR spectroscopy, the wavenumber (cm-1) of the light is directly proportional to its frequency & inversely proportional to its wavelength (λ). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 20 / search: "frequency is inversely proportional to wavelength the graph"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 35 of 59 / search: "frequency inversely wavelength"
- In mass spectrometry, charged particles with stronger magnetic fields (B) have a smaller radius of curvature. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 45 of 59 / search: "charged particles smaller"
- In mass spectrometry, particles with larger charges (q) have a smaller radius of curvature. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 45 of 59 / search: "particles charges smaller"
- In NMR spectroscopy, the x-axis represents chemical shift (δ), with the units parts per million (ppm). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 30 of 59 / search: "expressed in parts per million ppm which is"
- In normal-phase chromatography, the stationary phase is polar & the mobile phase is non-polar. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 44 of 59 / search: "phase chromatography stationary"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 59 / search: "chromatography stationary mobile"
- In reverse-phase chromatography, the stationary phase is non-polar & the mobile phase is polar. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 44 of 59 / search: "phase chromatography stationary"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 59 / search: "chromatography stationary mobile"
- In reverse-phase Paper/TLC, the plate is non-polar & the solvent is polar. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 47 of 59 / search: "phase polar solvent"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 49 of 59 / search: "phase polar solvent"
- In UV spectroscopy, electrons with small energy gaps between their highest-occupied orbital (HOMO) & lowest unoccupied orbital (LUMO) are easier to excite. -> Local sources: 06-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q.pdf / Question 23 of 30 / search: "electrons occupied orbital"; 08-UWorld_Physics_05212026_ID411469881_30Q-Results-Merge.pdf / Question 23 of 30 / search: "electrons occupied orbital"
- NMR spectroscopy uses magnetic fields to orient the nuclear spins of certain protons in the same (α) or opposite (β) direction - which get excited by radiofrequency irradiations. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "nuclear protons beta"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 36 of 59 / search: "uses magnetic fields"
- Paper chromatography uses cellulose as the medium for its stationary phase. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 44 of 59 / search: "chromatography stationary phase"
- The transition of an electron from a π-orbital → π*-orbital means the electron is becoming excited. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 5 / search: "electron orbital means"
- The transition of an electron from a π*-orbital → π-orbital means the electron is relaxing to its ground state. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 5 / search: "electron orbital means"
- Thin-layer chromatography uses either silica or alumina as the medium for its stationary phase. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 44 of 59 / search: "chromatography stationary phase"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 10 / search: "monitored by thin layer chromatography tlc when the"
- When bonding electrons (π) absorb UV light, they get excited to the anti-bonding orbital (π*). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 5 / search: "electrons excited orbital"
- When non-bonding electrons (n) absorb UV light, they get excited to the anti-bonding orbital (π*). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 5 / search: "electrons excited orbital"

- "In alpha decay, α-particles are packets of helium atoms - containing 2 protons and 2 neutrons." -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "decay particles protons"; Circuits Discretes.docx / Question 3 / search: "a nuclear decay of device materials o b"

- "In gamma decay, the atomic numbers (Z) of daughter nuclei are unchanged & the mass numbers (A) are unchanged." -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "gamma decay atomic"
- beta+ decay is also called positron emission. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "beta decay emission"

## Psychology - Individuals Society.txt

- 5 factors of Merton's strain theory: 1. Conformity 2. Innovation 3. Ritualism 4. Retreatism 5. Rebellion -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Discretes.docx / Question 3 / search: "set of factors associated with an increased risk"
- According to symbolic interactionism, deviance can best be understood through everyday, person-to-person interactions. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 22 / search: "framework a symbolic interactionism b exchange rational choice"
- Formal norms are social norms written down in law, whereas informal norms are unspoken rules held by society. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 1 / search: "values and norms oppose those of mainstream society"
- In collective behavior, mass hysteria is when the general public panics in response to some potential threat. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Passage 7 / search: "high crime public housing project in a poverty"
- In collective behavior, riots are when large groups of people engage in deviant behavior, like vandalizing and destroying stores. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Passage 7 / search: "in a large urban area both children lived"
- In labeling theory, placing people into particular social groups eventually pressures them to act accordingly with that group. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 34 / search: "sick role theory which statement best describes a"
- In Merton's strain theory, conformity is when people pursue conventional goals (like getting rich) through socially acceptable means. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 34 / search: "sick role theory which statement best describes a"
- In Merton's strain theory, innovation is when people pursue conventional goals (like getting rich) through unconventional means. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 34 / search: "sick role theory which statement best describes a"
- In Merton's strain theory, rebellion is when people reject conventional goals and the typical means to get them - attempting to resist the convention. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 34 / search: "sick role theory which statement best describes a"
- In Merton's strain theory, retreatism is when people reject conventional goals and subsequently reject the conventional means to getting there - finding a way to escape it. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Discretes.docx / Question 3 / search: "adult this finding best reflects a the sick"; Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 34 / search: "sick role theory which statement best describes a"
- In Merton's strain theory, ritualism is when people reject conventional goals (like getting rich) but still follow the conventional means to getting there (working). -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 34 / search: "sick role theory which statement best describes a"
- Labeling theory is a deviance theory that says particular labels (i.e. stereotypes) are placed on certain groups of people regardless of their behaviors. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Discretes.docx / Question 46 / search: "violence when certain individuals experience a defeat they"; Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 34 / search: "sick role theory which statement best describes a"
- Learning deviant behavior from watching others supports the theory of differential association. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 6 of 20 / search: "learning behavior watching"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 30 / search: "learning behavior watching"
- Mass psychogenic illness can result in real symptoms, despite the symptoms being induced by fear. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Discretes.docx / Question 45 / search: "severe premenstrual symptoms with marked mood changes that"; Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 36 / search: "to mental illness is best demonstrated by a"
- Mass psychogenic illness is a form of mass hysteria where people believe they all came down with the same illness despite being healthy. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 34 / search: "o b people holding loved ones with bd"
- Mores are social norms that are based in morality & are deemed necessary for society - resulting in minor consequences when they're violated. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 1 / search: "values and norms oppose those of mainstream society"
- Negative sanctions are punishments given to people for violating social norms, like sending someone to jail. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Passage 6 / search: "more producers people age 15 64 than elderly"
- Norms are the standards set by society that dictate which behaviors are normal or abnormal. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 1 / search: "values and norms oppose those of mainstream society"; Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 34 / search: "of a society s failure to exempt individuals"
- Social control theory says that a person's social groups (friends, family, relationships) encourage them to resist temptations to break the law. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Discretes.docx / Question 46 / search: "toward a family member which of the following"; Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 2 / search: "when social control gradually shifts from religion to"
- Social disorganization theory takes a look at how inadequate social institutions can influence people to engage in deviant behavior. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 30 / search: "takes engage behavior"; Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 34 / search: "sick role theory which statement best describes a"
- The theory of differential association says deviance is learned by surrounding yourself with others that regularly violate norms. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Passage 1 / search: "and rituals surrounding the sacred and provides meaning"; Demographics Social Structure Discretes.docx / Question 46 / search: "found an association between situational stress and intrafamily"
- What's the difference between mobs & riots? Mobs: large violent crowd targeting specific people (i.e. dictators). ## Psychology - Memory.txt

- As you get older, your semantic memory improves until around age 60. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Passage 6 / search: "population growth around 1860 the u s birth"

- Operation span is a test that measures an individual's working memory by asking them to repeat words in a specific order while answering math questions. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Discretes.docx / Question 20 / search: "heart disease while overlooking the role of social"
- People are better able to recall the central details of flashbulb memories while forgetting the peripheral details, since increased emotional arousal shifts our focus onto the event's central features. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 20 of 30 / search: "recall details flashbulb"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 58 of 59 / search: "peripheral since features"
- Pre-synaptic neurons becoming better at making stronger post-synaptic connections is the basis of learning. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 38 / search: "the quote better reflects a stigmatized approach to"
- Recovered memories are memories that were initially repressed during childhood but later emerged in adulthood - usually viewed as false memories created by outside influences. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Discretes.docx / Question 20 / search: "promotion of false consciousness in popular media a"; Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Question 49 / search: "class in adulthood o b positively correlated with"
- Retroactive interference relies on information stored in your short-term memory. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 20 / search: "information in short term memory which has a"
- Short-term memory is memory for an event that occurred less than 20 seconds ago. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 20 / search: "information in short term memory which has a"
- The amygdala is involved in the formation of highly emotional memories into long-term memory. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 20 of 30 / search: "emotional memories term"

Long-term memory store -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 20 / search: "information in short term memory which has a"

- The misinformation effect says that our episodic memory of an event becomes less accurate after learning new post-event information. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Discretes.docx / Question 48 / search: "statement is accurate regarding research designed to test"
- The primacy & recency effects are collectively called the serial position effect. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 14 of 30 / search: "primacy recency serial"
- The primacy effect relies on long-term memory, and the recency effect relies on short-term memory. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 20 / search: "information in short term memory which has a"
- The primacy effect says we'll remember information towards the beginning of a list easier than the middle. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 14 of 30 / search: "primacy remember beginning"
- The recency effect relies on short-term memory, and the primacy effect relies on long-term memory. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 20 / search: "information in short term memory which has a"
- The recency effect says we'll remember information towards the end of a list easier than the middle. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 14 of 30 / search: "recency remember list"

- Gestalt's law of symmetry says that we tend to perceive stimuli as being symmetrical around a central point. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "perceive stimuli point"
- In psychophysics, the descending method of limit is when a stimulus is administered at a detectable level & gets gradually decreased until the participant is no longer aware of it. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Passage 6 / search: "steadily decline until reaching its current plateau of"
- In psychophysics, the method of constant stimulation is when the stimulus is administered at random intervals during the testing period to avoid expectations. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Passages.docx / Passage 3 / search: "roles and expectations for both males and females"
- In sensory adaptation, changes in our proprioception were experimented on by goggles that flipped vision upside-down. What happened next? Their eyes eventually adapted to the goggles and flipped vision back to the proper orientation. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "sensory adaptation vision"
- In sensory adaptation, how does our sense of smell adapt to odors? Sensory receptors in our nose becomes desensitized to the odor molecules - eventually stop being able to smell it. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "sensory adaptation odor"
- In sensory adaptation, how does our sense of touch adapt to temperature? Thermoreceptors in our hands become desensitized and stop firing after some time. We perceive... water feels hot → water stops feeling hot. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 12 of 59 / search: "hands become feels"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 13 of 59 / search: "hands become feels"
- In sensory adaptation, how is our vision able to adapt to changes in light? Bright outside... pupils constrict Dark outside... pupils dilate -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "sensory adaptation vision"
- In signal detection theory, conservative strategies are when you always say no unless you're 100% confident the signal is there. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 10 / search: "only the signal detection theory quantifies how judgments"
- In signal detection theory, liberal strategies are when you always say yes, the signal is there. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 10 / search: "only the signal detection theory quantifies how judgments"

- In somatosensation, how frequently do non-adapting neurons fire action potentials? Fire consistently -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 30 / search: "neurons action potentials"
- In somatosensation, how frequently do slow-adapting neurons fire action potentials? A lot at first → slows down. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 30 / search: "neurons action potentials"

## Psychology - Vision.txt

- "Negative afterimages are illusions where we ""see"" the opposing color components of an image when we close our eyes after focusing on the image." -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Discretes.docx / Question 19 / search: "immigrants of color experience poorer health overall the"
- Feature detection refers to how only particular neurons fire in response to certain stimuli (visual, auditory, etc.) in order for us to process them. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "feature detection neurons"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 10 / search: "detection visual auditory"
- In the eye, the fovea is dimpled inward. What benefit does this serve? Allows light to come into direct contact with cones instead of having to pass through nerve axons -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 6 / search: "not in direct contact with the surrounding environment"
- In the magnocellular pathway, signals from the retina travel to the lateral geniculate nucleus → primary visual cortex → posterior of cortex. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 18 of 30 / search: "center called the lateral geniculate nucleus lgn in"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 19 of 30 / search: "center called the lateral geniculate nucleus lgn in"
- In the parvocellular pathway, signals from the retina travel to the lateral geniculate nucleus → primary visual cortex → anterior of cortex. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 18 of 30 / search: "center called the lateral geniculate nucleus lgn in"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 19 of 30 / search: "center called the lateral geniculate nucleus lgn in"

- The bipolar cells that transmit information from our rods & cones are supported by horizontal cells, which help detect visual contrasts. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 10 / search: "our detect visual"
- The Hermann grid illusion is an illusion where we see black dots at the intersections of white lines on a black-and-white grid. -> Local sources: Demographics Social Structure Discretes.docx / Question 1 / search: "exporting goods black bars and exporting resources white"
- The optic tracts carry signals from the optic nerve past the optic chiasma to reach the brain. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 10 / search: "tracts carry reach"
- The retina contains both rods and cones. Where are the rods & cones located (respectively) on the retina? On the retina... Center: cones Periphery: rods -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 24 of 30 / search: "retina located center"
- Visual information from an object in our right or left field of vision is processed in both hemisphere(s). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 28 of 30 / search: "visual left field"
- Visual information from the left-side components of the object in each right and left visual field are processed in the right hemisphere. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 28 of 30 / search: "the patients left visual field he is unable"
- Visual information from the right-side components of the object in each right and left visual field are processed in the left hemisphere. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 28 of 30 / search: "the patients left visual field he is unable"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 20 / search: "the body the left hemisphere controls touch and"
